<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>Fiscal 2002 Compared to Fiscal 2001  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Net sales in the year ended December&nbsp;28, 2002 were $1.27&nbsp;billion, an increase of 11.4% over the year ended December&nbsp;29, 2001 sales of
$1.14&nbsp;billion. The increase was due to an increase in comparable store sales of 4.8% and the inclusion of 31 stores opened during 2001 for the entire 2002 period and 28 net new stores opened in
2002. The increase in comparable store sales was primarily attributable to improved pharmacy sales, which increased to 41.8% of total sales in 2002 compared to 39.2% of total sales in 2001. Pharmacy
sales have followed the general industry trend reflecting accelerated growth rates versus front-end sales. Pharmacy comparable store sales increased by 12.1%, while front-end
comparable store sales were flat. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Cost
of sales as a percentage of net sales increased to 77.5% for 2002 from 76.2% for 2001, resulting in a decrease in gross profit margin to 22.5% for 2002 from 23.8% for 2001. The
gross margin decline primarily resulted from the absence of comparable store growth in the higher margin front-end sales and the faster growth rate of lower margin pharmacy sales. The
absence of growth in comparable front-end sales for the year was primarily attributable to the recessionary economy which pervaded the metro New York market throughout 2002. Gross profit
was also adversely impacted by higher shrink related losses. In addition, for 2002 and 2001, cost of sales includes other related real estate income and income from the sale of market related data
totaling $5.5&nbsp;million and $10.6&nbsp;million, respectively. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Selling,
general and administrative expenses were $198.5&nbsp;million, or 15.6% of net sales, and $173.0&nbsp;million, or 15.1% of net sales, in 2002 and 2001, respectively. The
increase as a percentage of sales reflects a lower rate of same store sales growth in fiscal 2002 than in 2001, increased labor costs and operating leases associated with the startup of 65 incremental
one hour photo processing </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>19</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<!-- ZEQ.=2,SEQ=19,EFW="2106462",CP="DUANE READE INC.",DN="1",CHK=1004687,FOLIO='19',FILE='DISK030:[03NYC7.03NYC3347]DE3347A.;22',USER='SMENEZE',CD='28-MAR-2003;12:24' -->
<A NAME="page_de3347_1_20"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>
departments, higher costs of property insurance in the aftermath of the September&nbsp;11 disaster and increased legal and litigation-related expenses. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Depreciation
and amortization of intangibles in 2002 and 2001 was $26.9&nbsp;million and $26.6&nbsp;million, respectively. The increase was attributable to capital spending for
property and equipment additions during 2001 and 2002, primarily in support of new store growth as well as amortization expenses for pharmacy customer lists and lease acquisition costs for
acquisitions completed during 2001 and 2002.
Fiscal 2002 also reflects a benefit of approximately $4.3&nbsp;million due to the elimination of goodwill amortization, attributable to our adoption of Financial Accounting Standard No.&nbsp;142. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Store
pre-opening expenses of $2.1&nbsp;million related to the opening of 32 stores in 2002 as compared to $1.7&nbsp;million reflecting 31 store openings in 2001. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Net
interest expense decreased to $17.9&nbsp;million in 2002 from $27.6&nbsp;million in 2001. The decrease in interest expense was principally due to the $210.5&nbsp;million of
proceeds from the April&nbsp;2002 Convertible Note Offering that were used to reduce higher cost term loan, revolver and 9<SUP>1</SUP>/<SMALL>4</SMALL>% Senior Subordinated Note borrowings. In addition, we
realized lower interest rates on the floating rate portion of our revolving credit facility during 2002. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Our
pre-tax income increased 15.8% to $50.3&nbsp;million in 2002 from $43.5&nbsp;million in 2001. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;During
2002, we recorded an income tax provision of $18.9&nbsp;million, reflecting an effective tax rate of 40.9%, reduced by certain wage-related income tax credits
amounting to $1.7&nbsp;million. During 2001, we recorded an income tax provision of $17.2&nbsp;million, reflecting an effective tax rate of 43.0%, reduced by wage-related income tax
credits totaling $1.4&nbsp;million. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;During
2002, we recorded total net extraordinary charges of $6.6&nbsp;million, net of an income tax benefit of $4.7&nbsp;million, which were composed of the following:
(1)&nbsp;$1.8&nbsp;million, reflecting the accelerated amortization of deferred financing costs related to (a)&nbsp;loans under our Senior Credit Agreement that were repaid with the proceeds of
our offering of senior convertible notes, (b)&nbsp;our 9<SUP>1</SUP>/<SMALL>4</SMALL>% Senior Subordinated Notes that were purchased pursuant to a tender offer completed in June&nbsp;2002, and (c)&nbsp;the
December 2002 repurchase of a portion of our senior convertible notes, (2)&nbsp;$4.1&nbsp;million associated with the payment of consent premiums and other expenses related to the tender offer,
(3)&nbsp;$2.3&nbsp;million related to the termination of the interest rate swap agreement tied to interest expenses on the loans under the Senior Credit Agreement that were retired with proceeds
from the convertible notes offering, and (4)&nbsp;an extraordinary gain of $1.6&nbsp;million related to the December 2002 repurchase of $17.5&nbsp;million of our outstanding senior convertible
notes. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;During
2002, as a result of the change in accounting method for inventory valuation from retail dollar FIFO to specific cost LIFO, we recorded a one-time,
non-cash charge of $9.3&nbsp;million, net of an income tax benefit of $6.7&nbsp;million. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Net
income was $15.6&nbsp;million in 2002 and $24.7&nbsp;million in 2001. The decrease was due to the factors previously described. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>Fiscal 2001 Compared to Fiscal 2000  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Net sales in the 52-week year ended December&nbsp;29, 2001 were $1.14&nbsp;billion, an increase of 14.3% over the 53-week year ended
December&nbsp;30, 2000 sales of $1.00&nbsp;billion. On a comparable 52-week basis, net sales in 2001 increased 16.3% over the same period in 2000. The increases were due to increased
comparable store sales of 6.3% and the inclusion of 24 stores opened during 2000 for the entire 2001 period and 28 net new stores opened in 2001. The increase in comparable store sales was primarily
attributable to improved pharmacy sales, which increased to 39.2% of total sales in 2001 compared to 35.4% of total sales in 2000. Pharmacy sales have followed the general industry trend reflecting
accelerated growth rates versus front-end sales. Pharmacy and front-end comparable sales increased by 16.6% and 0.6%, respectively. </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>20</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<!-- ZEQ.=3,SEQ=20,EFW="2106462",CP="DUANE READE INC.",DN="1",CHK=947834,FOLIO='20',FILE='DISK030:[03NYC7.03NYC3347]DE3347A.;22',USER='SMENEZE',CD='28-MAR-2003;12:24' -->
<A NAME="page_de3347_1_21"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Cost
of sales as a percentage of net sales increased to 76.2% for 2001 from 74.6% for 2000, resulting in a decrease in gross profit margin to 23.8% for 2001 from 25.4% for 2000. Cost of
goods sold in 2001 includes two unusual items, a loss of $2.6&nbsp;million from the early termination of a supply agreement and a gain of $1.4&nbsp;million from the sale of a few stores' customer
lists. The combined net loss of $1.2&nbsp;million for these unusual items represented 0.1% of sales in 2001. The balance of the gross margin decline primarily resulted from the low
front-end comparable store growth rate of 0.6% and the faster growth rate of lower margin pharmacy sales. The low growth rate in comparable front-end sales for the year was
primarily attributable to the impact of customer disruptions in the aftermath of the World Trade Center disaster, the recessionary economy in the second half of the year and a mild flu season in the
fourth quarter that depressed sales of cough and cold categories. Lower margin pharmacy sales benefited in the fourth quarter from increased demand for ciprofloxacin as a result of anthrax scares, as
well as higher rates of sales in certain sleep aids and anti-depressants. Gross profit was also adversely impacted by the loss of front-end sales related allowances in the
period following the World Trade Center disaster. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Selling,
general and administrative expenses were $173.0&nbsp;million, or 15.1% of net sales, and $155.6&nbsp;million, or 15.6% of net sales, in 2001 and 2000, respectively. The
decrease as a percentage of sales reflects improved efficiencies and additional expense leveraging against new store sales, as well as a reduction in earnings-based incentive compensation and benefit
costs. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Depreciation
and amortization of intangibles in 2001 and 2000 was $26.6&nbsp;million and $23.2&nbsp;million, respectively. The increase was attributable to capital spending for
property and equipment additions during 2000 and 2001, primarily in support of new store growth as well as amortization expenses for goodwill, pharmacy customer lists and lease acquisition costs for
acquisitions completed during 2000 and 2001. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Store
pre-opening expenses of $1.7&nbsp;million related to the opening of 31 stores in 2001 as compared to $1.4&nbsp;million reflecting 24 store openings in 2000. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Net
interest expense decreased to $27.6&nbsp;million in 2001 from $35.9&nbsp;million in 2000. The decrease in interest expense was principally due to the $130.4&nbsp;million of
proceeds from the June, 2001 Equity Offering that were used to reduce term loan and revolver borrowings and lower interest rates on the floating rate portion of our revolving credit facility during
2001, as well as one less week in fiscal 2001 as compared to fiscal 2000. This was partially offset by increased revolver borrowings attributable to the lost sales and earnings in the aftermath of the
World Trade Center disaster. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Our
pre-tax income increased 13.5% to $43.5&nbsp;million in 2001 from $38.3&nbsp;million in 2000. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;During
2001, we recorded an income tax provision of $17.2&nbsp;million, reflecting an effective tax rate of 43.0%, reduced by certain wage-related income tax credits
amounting to $1.4&nbsp;million. During 2000, we recorded an income tax provision of $15.6&nbsp;million, reflecting an effective tax rate of 42.9%, reduced by wage-related income tax
credits totaling $0.8&nbsp;million. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Net
income was $24.7&nbsp;million in 2001 and $22.7&nbsp;million in 2000. The increase of $2.0&nbsp;million is a result of the increase in pre-tax income of
$5.2&nbsp;million in 2001 versus 2000, partially offset by the incremental income tax provision of $1.6&nbsp;million and the after-tax extraordinary charge of $1.5&nbsp;million in
2001, reflecting the write-off of deferred financing costs as a result of the June 2001 early retirement of debt. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>Liquidity and Capital Resources  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On April&nbsp;16, 2002, we completed an offering (the "2002 Offering") of $381.5&nbsp;million aggregate principal amount of senior convertible notes maturing
on April&nbsp;16, 2022 (the "Convertible Notes"). After deducting commissions and expenses related to the offering, we realized net proceeds of $210.5&nbsp;million. A portion of the proceeds was
used to repay an aggregate of approximately $86.1&nbsp;million in principal amount of Term A loans and Term B loans and $41.5&nbsp;million in principal </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>21</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<!-- ZEQ.=4,SEQ=21,EFW="2106462",CP="DUANE READE INC.",DN="1",CHK=377633,FOLIO='21',FILE='DISK030:[03NYC7.03NYC3347]DE3347A.;22',USER='SMENEZE',CD='28-MAR-2003;12:24' -->
<A NAME="page_de3347_1_22"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>
amount of revolving loans (which revolving loans may be reborrowed) under our Senior Credit Agreement. In addition, we terminated an interest rate swap agreement, which was set to expire in
January&nbsp;2003, at a cost of approximately $3.9&nbsp;million. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The
Convertible Notes were issued at a discount and pay cash interest at the rate of 2.1478% per year on the principal amount at maturity, until April&nbsp;16, 2007. After that date,
interest will accrue on the notes as amortization of the original issue discount representing a yield to maturity of 3.75% per year, computed on a semi-annual bond equivalent basis.
Holders of the Convertible Notes may convert each $1,000 in principal amount of their Convertible Notes into 14.1265 shares of our common stock, subject to adjustment, only if (1)&nbsp;the sale
price of our common stock reaches, or the trading price of the notes falls below, specified thresholds, (2)&nbsp;the notes are called for redemption, or (3)&nbsp;specified corporate
transactions have occurred. Upon conversion, we have the right to deliver, in lieu of our common stock, cash or a combination of cash and common stock in an amount as described in the indenture. It is
our intention to redeem these notes by delivering cash. Holders of the Convertible Notes may require us to purchase all or a portion of their notes on April&nbsp;16, 2007 at a price of $572.76 per
note plus accrued cash interest, if any; on April&nbsp;16, 2012 at a price of $689.68 per note plus accrued cash interest, if any; and on April&nbsp;16, 2017 at a price of $830.47 per note plus
accrued cash interest, if any. We may choose to pay the purchase price of such notes in cash or common stock or a combination of cash and common stock. In addition, if we experience a change in
control, each holder may require us to purchase for cash all or a portion of such holder's notes at a price equal to the sum of the issue price plus accrued original issue discount and accrued cash
interest, if any, to the date of purchase. We may redeem for cash all or a portion of the Convertible Notes at any time after April&nbsp;16, 2007, at a price equal to the sum of the issue price plus
accrued original issue discount and accrued cash interest, if any, to the redemption date. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On
June&nbsp;3, 2002, we completed a tender offer and consent solicitation (the "Tender Offer") to purchase our outstanding 9<SUP>1</SUP>/<SMALL>4</SMALL>% Senior Subordinated Notes due 2008 (the
"Senior Notes"). On June&nbsp;3, 2002, we expended a total of $87.1&nbsp;million from the balance of the proceeds of the 2002 Offering to pay our obligations under the Tender Offer. This payment
was composed of principal value ($78.4&nbsp;million), premium payments ($6.5&nbsp;million) and accrued interest earned from February&nbsp;16, 2002 through the payment date ($2.2&nbsp;million).
During the fourth quarter of 2002, we repurchased and retired $17.5&nbsp;million of the Convertible Notes at a cost of $14.9&nbsp;million, resulting in an extraordinary gain, prior to the effect
of income taxes, of $2.6&nbsp;million. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;At
December&nbsp;28, 2002, we had $4.8&nbsp;million in Term A and $60.3&nbsp;million in Term B loans outstanding under our Senior Credit Agreement, $201.0&nbsp;million of
outstanding Convertible Notes and $1.6&nbsp;million of outstanding Senior Notes. We had no outstanding borrowings under our $80.0&nbsp;million revolving credit facility (other than
$0.8&nbsp;million of outstanding standby letters of credit) and $4.2&nbsp;million in cash. On February&nbsp;18, 2003 we retired the remaining $1.6&nbsp;million of Senior Notes. Any amounts
outstanding under our revolving loans and Term A loans mature on February&nbsp;15, 2004 and the Term B loans mature on February&nbsp;15, 2007. Our outstanding borrowings under the Senior Credit
Agreement are principally LIBOR based borrowings with margins of 1.75% on revolver and Term A loans and a margin of 2.50% on Term B loans. We are currently evaluating proposals for refinancing our
Senior Credit Agreement and expect to replace the Agreement with a longer term maturity financing during the current year. We expect that the interest rates we obtain upon the refinancing of these
loans will be approximately equivalent to the rates currently in effect. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The
Senior Credit Agreement contains various covenants that limit or restrict, among other things, subject to certain exceptions, our ability to make capital expenditures, incur
indebtedness, permit liens on our property, enter into transactions with affiliates, make restricted payments, investments or acquisitions, enter into mergers, consolidations or dissolutions, conduct
asset sales, pay dividends or distributions and enter into other specified transactions and business activities. Financial performance covenants included in our Senior Credit Agreement include
interest coverage, leverage ratios, minimum net worth requirements and fixed charge coverage requirements. At December&nbsp;28, 2002, we were in </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>22</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<!-- ZEQ.=5,SEQ=22,EFW="2106462",CP="DUANE READE INC.",DN="1",CHK=1035831,FOLIO='22',FILE='DISK030:[03NYC7.03NYC3347]DE3347A.;22',USER='SMENEZE',CD='28-MAR-2003;12:24' -->
<A NAME="page_de3347_1_23"> </A>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>
compliance with all financial performance covenants in our Senior Credit Agreement. There are no credit ratings related triggers in our Senior Credit Agreement or in the indenture related to our
Convertible Notes that would impact cost of borrowing, annual amortization of principal or related debt maturities. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Working
capital was $230.9&nbsp;million as of December&nbsp;28, 2002 and $214.1&nbsp;million as of December&nbsp;29, 2001. The increase of $16.8&nbsp;million was primarily due
to an increase in accounts receivable of $4.9&nbsp;million combined with a decrease of $7.1&nbsp;million in accrued interest and the current portion of long-term debt. The increase in
accounts receivable primarily reflects the growth of the third-party pharmacy business. The change in accrued interest and the current portion of long-term debt is reflective of the
restructuring of our debt, including the liquidation of our Senior Notes and the accelerated repayment of a portion of our outstanding term loans. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;For
fiscal 2002, net cash provided by operating activities was $42.5&nbsp;million, compared to $25.8&nbsp;million for fiscal 2001. The primary reason for the increase was the lower
rate of growth in working capital in 2002 over 2001 than experienced in 2001 over 2000. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;For
fiscal 2002, net cash used in investing activities was $60.5&nbsp;million, compared to $48.1&nbsp;million in fiscal 2001. Net cash used in investing activities in 2002 was for
capital expenditures of $47.6&nbsp;million, primarily related to the opening and remodeling of new and renovated stores, combined with $12.9&nbsp;million for lease, pharmacy file and other
acquisition costs. Net cash used in investing activities in 2001 was due to capital expenditures of $41.0&nbsp;million and $8.5&nbsp;million for lease, pharmacy file and other acquisition costs,
partially offset by $1.4&nbsp;million of proceeds generated by the sale of certain stores' pharmacy customer files. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;For
fiscal 2002, net cash provided by financing activities was $17.2&nbsp;million, compared to $26.3&nbsp;million in fiscal 2001. The lower levels of cash provided by financing
activities in 2002 resulted from the improved level of cash flow from operating activities partially offset by increased capital expenditures to support increased levels of new store growth and higher
levels of cash spending for lease, pharmacy file and other acquisition costs. Proceeds of $210.5&nbsp;million from the 2002 Offering were used to repay a portion of our outstanding senior debt. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Our
capital requirements primarily result from opening and stocking new stores, remodeling and renovating existing retail locations and from the continuing development of management
information systems. We believe that there are significant opportunities to open additional stores, and currently plan to open approximately 35 to 45 stores during the next two years. We expect to
spend approximately $40.0&nbsp;million in fiscal 2003 on capital expenditures, primarily for new and replacement stores and an additional $13.0&nbsp;million for lease and pharmacy file
acquisitions and other costs. We also require working capital to support inventory for our existing stores. Historically, we have been able to lease our store locations. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Leases
for 13 of our stores that generated approximately 4.2% of our net sales for fiscal 2002 are scheduled to expire before the end of fiscal 2004. Four of these leases have renewal
options. We
believe that we will be able to renew the other expiring leases on economically favorable terms or, alternatively, find other economically attractive locations to lease. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;As
of December&nbsp;28, 2002, approximately 4,600 of our approximately 6,000 employees were represented by various labor unions and were covered by collective bargaining agreements.
Pursuant to the terms of the collective bargaining agreements covering these employees, we are required, in some instances, to pay specified annual increases in salary and benefits contributions
relating to the member employees. We do not believe that these increases will have a material impact on our liquidity or results of operations. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Under
an employment agreement with our Chairman and CEO negotiated during fiscal 2002, we are required to fund premiums for a split dollar life insurance policy that will provide certain
post-retirement benefits. During fiscal 2002 these premiums amounted to $4.0&nbsp;million and are </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>23</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<!-- ZEQ.=6,SEQ=23,EFW="2106462",CP="DUANE READE INC.",DN="1",CHK=346051,FOLIO='23',FILE='DISK030:[03NYC7.03NYC3347]DE3347A.;22',USER='SMENEZE',CD='28-MAR-2003;12:24' -->
<A NAME="page_de3347_1_24"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>
scheduled to increase to $5.0&nbsp;million per year in fiscal 2003 through 2010. The premiums have been established at a level anticipated to be sufficient to cover the full amount of the projected
retirement benefits as well as to return the full cost of the premiums, plus a 3% rate of interest. Recent Sarbanes-Oxley legislation has resulted in the need for additional guidance concerning the
permissibility of split dollar life insurance policies for executives. While we believe this split dollar policy is permitted under current interpretations of the legislation, there can be no
assurance that future interpretations or guidance to be provided by the SEC concerning this legislation will concur. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;We
believe that, based on current levels of operations and anticipated growth, cash flow from operations, together with other available sources of funds, including revolving loan
borrowings subject to an extension, refinancing or replacement of our Senior Credit Agreement, will be adequate for at least the next two years to make required payments of principal and interest on
our indebtedness, to fund anticipated capital expenditures and to satisfy our working capital requirements. Our ability to meet our debt service obligations and reduce our total debt will depend upon
our future performance which, in turn, will be subject to general economic, financial, business, competitive, legislative, regulatory and other conditions, many of which are beyond our control. In
addition, we cannot assure you that our operating results, cash flow and capital resources will be sufficient for repayment of our indebtedness in the future. Substantially all of our borrowings under
the Senior Credit Agreement bear interest at floating rates. Therefore, our financial condition will be affected by changes in prevailing interest rates. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;We
are party to multi-year, merchandise supply agreements in the normal course of business. The largest of these is with AmerisourceBergen, our primary pharmaceutical
supplier. Generally, these agreements provide for certain volume commitments and are terminable by us, subject in some cases to specified termination payments, none of which would constitute a
material adverse effect on our financial position, results of operations or cash flows. It is the opinion of management that if any of these agreements were terminated or if any contracting party was
to experience events precluding fulfillment of its obligations, we would be able to find a suitable alternative supplier. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;We
are not a party to any agreements with, or commitments to, any special purpose entities that would constitute material off balance sheet financing other than the operating lease
commitments listed above. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>Critical Accounting Policies  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Our discussion of results of operations and financial condition relies on our consolidated financial statements that are prepared based on certain critical
accounting policies that require management to make judgments and estimates that are subject to varying degrees of uncertainty. We believe that investors need to be aware of these policies and how
they impact our financial reporting to gain a more complete understanding of our consolidated financial statements as a whole, as well as our related discussion and analysis presented herein. While we
believe that these accounting policies are grounded on sound measurement criteria, actual future events can and often do result in outcomes that can be materially different from these estimates or
forecasts. The accounting policies and related risks described in the paragraphs below are those that depend most heavily on these judgments and estimates. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><B>Pharmacy Receivables&#151;Reserves for Uncollectible Accounts&#151;</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>At December&nbsp;28, 2002, accounts receivable included
$33.5&nbsp;million of amounts due from various insurance companies and governmental agencies under third party payment plans for prescription sales made prior to the year-end date. Our
accounting policy is to fully reserve for all unpaid pharmacy receivables over 120&nbsp;days old, as well as any others deemed potentially uncollectible. This policy is based on our past collection
experience. Our uncollectible pharmacy receivable losses amounted to $1.2&nbsp;million in fiscal 2002 and there was approximately $3.8&nbsp;million reserved for uncollectible pharmacy receivables
at December&nbsp;28, 2002. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><B>Inventory Shrink Estimates&#151;</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>We take complete physical inventories in all of our stores at least once per year and
front-end physical inventories in most stores twice per year on a staggered cycle basis. We take physical inventories at our distribution centers twice per year. Front-end
inventories at balance sheet dates are valued using the specific-cost, item-based last in, first out (LIFO) method reduced by estimated inventory shrink losses for the period
between the last physical inventory in each store and the balance sheet date. These shrink estimates are based on the latest chain-wide trends. At December&nbsp;28, 2002, a change in
this shrink estimate of 1.0% of front-end sales would impact current year pre-tax earnings by approximately $2.8&nbsp;million. </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>25</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<!-- ZEQ.=8,SEQ=25,EFW="2106462",CP="DUANE READE INC.",DN="1",CHK=127935,FOLIO='25',FILE='DISK030:[03NYC7.03NYC3347]DE3347A.;22',USER='SMENEZE',CD='28-MAR-2003;12:24' -->
<A NAME="page_de3347_1_26"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><B>Insurance Liabilities and Reserves&#151;</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>At December&nbsp;28, 2002, there were $2.5&nbsp;million of accrued general liability
claim costs that primarily related to our self-insured portion of customer accident claims. Our policy is to recognize a liability for the estimated self-insured portion of the
projected ultimate settlement value of these claims as well as a provision for incurred but unreported claims as of each balance sheet date. These estimates are made based on a review of the facts and
circumstances of each individual claim using experienced third party claims adjustors. These estimates are also reviewed and monitored on an ongoing basis by management. For the vast majority of
claims, the maximum self-insured portion of any individual claim amounts to $100,000, however, our historical claim settlement experience is significantly lower. At December&nbsp;28,
2002, there were 259 outstanding claims with an average projected settlement value of approximately $9,600, as compared to 172 outstanding claims with an average projected settlement value of $13,000
at December&nbsp;29, 2001. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><B>Impairment of Goodwill and Intangible Assets&#151;</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>At December&nbsp;28, 2002, goodwill, net of accumulated amortization, amounted
to approximately $160.4&nbsp;million. Other net intangible assets consisted of lease acquisition costs of $35.5&nbsp;million, customer lists of $21.1&nbsp;million and non-compete
agreements amounting to $1.5&nbsp;million. Our policy is to evaluate our intangible assets, exclusive of goodwill, for impairment as of each balance sheet date by comparing the expected undiscounted
cash flows from the underlying stores or assets over their remaining asset lives to the net intangible asset values. Any intangible asset for which the projected undiscounted cash flow is insufficient
to recover the asset's carrying value is considered impaired and would be written down to its net recoverable value. Such write-downs would result in a non-cash charge to earnings. Based
upon our anticipated future revenues and cash flows and the net intangible balances existing at December&nbsp;28, 2002, all stores are projected to recover their intangible asset values within their
useful lives. Goodwill is evaluated at least annually as required under Statement of Financial Accounting Standards No 142. We utilize the market capitalization of our common stock in performing the
required impairment test. Our most recent evaluation did not indicate any impairment of goodwill. However, we may be required to perform an interim impairment review if circumstances indicate that an
impairment may have occurred. These circumstances include, but are not limited to, a significant adverse change in legal factors or in the business climate, adverse action or assessment by a
regulator, unanticipated competition or the loss of key personnel. We may be required to recognize an impairment charge at the time an interim or future annual impairment review is performed,
depending in part on the value of our market capitalization. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><B>Other Loss Contingencies&#151;</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>Liabilities for loss contingencies are recorded when it is probable that a liability has been
incurred and the amount of the loss is reasonably estimable. Loss contingencies often take years to resolve and can involve complicated litigation matters and potential regulatory actions, the
outcomes of which are difficult to predict. At December&nbsp;28, 2002, we have recorded one loss contingency, representing our estimated portion of a potential settlement of an ongoing lawsuit
between various retailers and a delivery drivers union. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><B>Income Taxes&#151;</B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>Our effective tax rate, which was 37.5% for the fiscal year ended December&nbsp;28, 2002, has been and is
expected to continue to be a major factor in the determination of our profitability and cash flow. As such, a significant shift in the relative sources of our earnings, or changes in tax rules or
interpretations, could have a material adverse effect on our results of operations and cash flow. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>Change in Accounting Method  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;During the first quarter of 2002, we adopted a change in accounting method to convert from the retail dollar based first-in, first-out
("FIFO") method of inventory valuation to an item specific cost based last-in, first-out ("LIFO") method of inventory valuation. This change resulted in a one-time
non-cash after tax charge of approximately $9.3&nbsp;million, which was recorded in the first quarter as the cumulative effect of an accounting change. Adoption of the specific cost LIFO
method has resulted in </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>26</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<!-- ZEQ.=9,SEQ=26,EFW="2106462",CP="DUANE READE INC.",DN="1",CHK=352449,FOLIO='26',FILE='DISK030:[03NYC7.03NYC3347]DE3347A.;22',USER='SMENEZE',CD='28-MAR-2003;12:24' -->
<A NAME="page_de3347_1_27"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>
the recognition of the latest item costs in our reported gross margins, and has made our results more comparable to other major retailers in our industry. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>Seasonality  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The non-pharmacy business is seasonal in nature, with the Christmas holiday season generating a higher proportion of sales and earnings than other
periods. See Note&nbsp;23 to the Consolidated Financial Statements for our quarterly results and an indication of our results of operations. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>Inflation  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;We believe that inflation has not had a material impact on our results of operations during the three years ended December&nbsp;28, 2002. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>Recently Issued Accounting Pronouncements  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;During the third quarter of 2001, we adopted Financial Accounting Standards Board Pronouncements Nos. 141 (FAS&nbsp;141) and 142 (FAS&nbsp;142) "Business
Combinations" and "Goodwill and Other Intangible Assets", respectively, for acquisitions completed after June&nbsp;30, 2001 (See Note 5 "Acquisitions"). These adoptions did not have a material
impact on our results of operations, financial position or cash flows. During the first quarter ended March&nbsp;30, 2002, we adopted these same standards for goodwill related to acquisitions
completed prior to July&nbsp;1, 2001. For the 52 weeks ended December&nbsp;28, 2002, our goodwill amortization expense was reduced by $4.3&nbsp;million as a result of the adoption of these
standards. Had these standards been adopted prior to the 2001 fiscal year, our net income for the 52 weeks ended December&nbsp;29, 2001 would have been approximately $27.3&nbsp;million. In
addition, for the 52 weeks ended December&nbsp;29, 2001, our net income per basic share outstanding and net income per diluted share outstanding would have been $1.30 and $1.25, respectively. At
December&nbsp;28, 2002, included within the "other assets" category on our balance sheet, were intangible assets totaling $71.5&nbsp;million, net of
accumulated amortization of $55.0&nbsp;million. The $71.5&nbsp;million is primarily composed of costs related to the acquisition of store leases ($35.5&nbsp;million) and pharmacy customer files
($21.1&nbsp;million), deferred financing costs ($7.3&nbsp;million) and all other net intangible assets ($7.6&nbsp;million). Lease acquisition costs are generally amortized over the remaining
lease life, pharmacy file acquisition costs are amortized over seven years, and deferred financing costs are amortized over the life of the financing agreement. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;During
the first quarter of 2002, we adopted Financial Accounting Standards Board Pronouncement No.&nbsp;144 (FAS&nbsp;144), "Accounting for the Impairment or Disposal of
Long-Lived Assets." FAS&nbsp;144 supersedes FAS&nbsp;121, "Accounting for the Impairment of Long-Lived Assets and for Long-Lived Assets to be Disposed of." The
provisions of FAS&nbsp;144 are effective for financial statements issued after December&nbsp;15, 2001. This adoption did not have a material impact on our results of operations, financial position
or cash flows (See Critical Accounting Policies above). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In
April&nbsp;2002, FAS No.&nbsp;145, "Rescission of FASB Statements No.&nbsp;4, 44, and 64, Amendment of FASB Statement No.&nbsp;13, and Technical Corrections," was issued.
Under FAS No.&nbsp;145, gains and losses related to the extinguishment of debt should no longer be segregated on the income statement as extraordinary items. Instead, such gains and losses should be
included as a component of income from continuing operations. The provisions of FAS No.&nbsp;145 are effective for fiscal years beginning after May&nbsp;15, 2002 with early adoption encouraged.
Upon adoption, we will reclassify from extraordinary charges to other income / (loss), for the fiscal years ended December&nbsp;28, 2002 and December&nbsp;29, 2001, pre-tax amounts of
$11.4&nbsp;million and $2.6&nbsp;million, respectively. The income tax provisions for the 2002 and 2001 fiscal years will be adjusted commensurately. Reported net income will remain unaffected by
the reclassification. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In
July&nbsp;2002, FAS No.&nbsp;146, "Accounting for Costs Associated with Exit or Disposal Activities," was issued. This statement nullifies Emerging Issues Task Force (EITF) Issue
No.&nbsp;94-3, "Liability </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>27</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<!-- ZEQ.=10,SEQ=27,EFW="2106462",CP="DUANE READE INC.",DN="1",CHK=949748,FOLIO='27',FILE='DISK030:[03NYC7.03NYC3347]DE3347A.;22',USER='SMENEZE',CD='28-MAR-2003;12:24' -->
<A NAME="page_de3347_1_28"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>
Recognition for Certain Employee Termination Benefits and Other Costs to Exit an Activity (including Certain Costs Incurred in a Restructuring)." FAS No.&nbsp;146 requires that a liability for
costs associated with an exit or disposal activity be recognized when the liability is incurred. The provisions of FAS No.&nbsp;146 are effective for exit or disposal activities initiated after
December&nbsp;31, 2002, with early adoption encouraged. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In
September&nbsp;2002, the Emerging Issues Task Force released Issue No.&nbsp;02-16, "Accounting by a Reseller for Cash Consideration Received from a Vendor". The
pronouncement addresses two issues. The first issue requires that vendor allowances be categorized as a reduction of cost of sales unless they are a reimbursement of costs incurred to sell the
vendor's products, in which case, the cash consideration should be characterized as a reduction of that cost. Cash consideration received from a vendor in excess of the fair value of the benefit
received should be characterized as a reduction of cost of sales. As required, we will adopt this portion of the pronouncement in 2003. The second issue requires that rebates or refunds payable only
if the customer completes a specified cumulative level of purchases should be recognized as a reduction of cost of sales based on a systematic and rational allocation over the purchase period. This
portion of the pronouncement is to be applied to all new arrangements initiated after November&nbsp;21, 2002. We do not expect that the adoption of this pronouncement will have a material impact on
our consolidated results of operations, financial position, or cash flows. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In
November&nbsp;2002, the Financial Accounting Standards Board issued FASB Interpretation (FIN) No.&nbsp;45, "Guarantor's Accounting and Disclosure Requirements for Guarantees,
Including Indirect Guarantees of Indebtedness of Others." FIN No.&nbsp;45 clarifies the requirements of FAS No.&nbsp;5, "Accounting for Contingencies," relating to a guarantor's accounting for and
disclosure of, the issuance of certain types of guarantees. FIN No.&nbsp;45 elaborates on the existing disclosure requirements for most guarantees, including loan guarantees such as standby letters
of credit. It also clarifies that at the time a company issues a guarantee, the company must recognize an initial liability for the fair value, or market value, of the obligations it assumes under the
guarantee and must disclose that information in its interim and annual financial statements. The provisions related to recognizing a liability at inception of the guarantee for the fair value of the
guarantor's obligations does not apply to product warranties or to guarantees accounted for as derivatives. The recognition provisions of FIN No.&nbsp;45 became effective for us beginning on
January&nbsp;1, 2003. We do not believe that this interpretation will have a material impact on our financial position, results of operations or cash flows. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In
December&nbsp;2002, SFAS No.&nbsp;148, "Accounting for Stock-Based Compensation&#151;Transition and Disclosure" was issued. This statement provides alternative methods of
transition for a voluntary change to the fair value based method of accounting for stock-based employee compensation. In addition, this statement amends the disclosure requirements of SFAS
No.&nbsp;123 to require prominent disclosures about the method of accounting for stock-based compensation and the effect of the method used on reported results. As required, we adopted SFAS
No.&nbsp;148 effective in 2002. The adoption did not have a material impact on our consolidated results of operations, financial position, or cash flows. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In
January&nbsp;2003, the Financial Accounting Standards Board issued FIN No.&nbsp;46, "Consolidation of Variable Interest Entities." FIN No.&nbsp;46 requires a variable interest
entity to be consolidated by a company if that company is subject to a majority of the risk of loss from the variable interest entity's activities or entitled to receive a majority of the entity's
residual returns or both. The consolidation requirements of FIN No.&nbsp;46 apply immediately to variable interest entities created after January&nbsp;31, 2003. The consolidation requirements
apply to older entities in the first fiscal year or interim period beginning after June&nbsp;15, 2003. Certain of the disclosure requirements apply in all financial statements issued after
January&nbsp;31, 2003, regardless of when the variable interest entity was established. We do not believe that the adoption of these provisions will have a material impact on our financial position,
results of operations or cash flows. </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>28</FONT></P>

<A NAME="page_de3347_1_29"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>ITEM 7A.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;QUANTITATIVE AND QUALITATIVE DISCUSSIONS ABOUT MARKET RISK  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Our financial results are subject to risk from interest rate fluctuations on debt which carries variable interest rates. Variable rate debt outstanding under our
Senior Credit Agreement was approximately $65.1&nbsp;million at December&nbsp;28, 2002. At December&nbsp;28, 2002, the weighted average combined interest rate in effect on all borrowings under
the Senior Credit Agreement was 4.32%. A 0.50% change in interest rates applied to the $65.1&nbsp;million balance of floating rate debt existing at December&nbsp;28, 2002 would
affect pre-tax annual results of operations by approximately $0.3&nbsp;million. In addition, we also have $201.0&nbsp;million of Convertible Notes and $1.6&nbsp;million of Senior
Notes outstanding at December&nbsp;28, 2002. These notes bear interest payable semi-annually at fixed rates of 3.75% and 9.25%, respectively, and are therefore not subject to risk from
interest rate fluctuations. The $1.6&nbsp;million of Senior Notes were retired on February&nbsp;18, 2003. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The
principal objective of our investment management activities is to maintain acceptable levels of interest rate and liquidity risk to facilitate our funding needs. As part of our risk
management, we may use derivative financial products such as interest rate hedges and interest rate swaps in the future. </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>29</FONT></P>

our opinion, the accompanying consolidated balance sheets and the related consolidated statements of operations, of stockholders' equity and of cash flows present fairly, in all material respects,
the financial position of Duane Reade,&nbsp;Inc. and its subsidiaries (the "Company") at December&nbsp;28, 2002 and December&nbsp;29, 2001 and the results of their operations and their cash
flows for each of the 52-week periods ended December&nbsp;28, 2002 and December&nbsp;29, 2001 and for the 53-week period ended December&nbsp;30, 2000, in conformity with accounting principles
generally accepted in the United States of America. These financial statements are the responsibility of the Company's management; our responsibility is to express an opinion on these financial
statements based on our audits. We conducted our audits of these statements in accordance with auditing standards generally accepted in the United States of America, which require that we plan and
perform the audit to obtain reasonable assurance about whether the financial statements are free of material misstatement. An audit includes examining, on a test basis, evidence supporting the amounts
and disclosures in the financial statements, assessing the accounting principles used and significant estimates made by management, and evaluating the overall financial statement presentation. We
believe that our audits provide a reasonable basis for our opinion. </FONT></P>

Other Intangible Assets." </FONT></P>

also described in Note&nbsp;1 to the consolidated financial statements, the Company has adopted the specific cost LIFO method of inventory accounting, effective December&nbsp;30, 2001. </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2><A
NAME="fj3347_duane_reade_inc._notes___fj302367"> </A>
<A NAME="toc_fj3347_1"> </A>
<BR></FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>DUANE READE&nbsp;INC.    <BR>    <BR>    Notes to Consolidated Financial Statements    <BR>    </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>1.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Organization and Summary of Significant Accounting Policies  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Duane Reade&nbsp;Inc. (the "Company") was formed on June&nbsp;16, 1992 as part of an acquisition of Duane Reade, a New York General Partnership and the
primary operating entity. The Company and a wholly owned subsidiary, DRI I&nbsp;Inc. ("DRI"), are general partners in Duane Reade. Duane Reade was originally founded in 1960 as a family-owned
business in the financial district of Manhattan in New York City. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The
Company was acquired in June of 1997 by certain affiliates of Donaldson, Lufkin and Jenrette (the "DLJ Entities"), and in February&nbsp;1998, the Company completed an initial
public offering of its common stock. In November&nbsp;2000, the ultimate parent of the DLJ Entities, DLJ&nbsp;Inc., was acquired by an indirect, wholly owned subsidiary of the Credit Suisse Group,
and on February&nbsp;1, 2001, Donaldson, Lufkin&nbsp;&amp; Jenrette Securities Corporation ("DLJ"), an affiliate of the DLJ Entities, changed its name to Credit Suisse First Boston Corporation
("CSFB"). CSFB subsequently reduced its ownership interest in common shares of the Company from 45.6% in December&nbsp;2000 to less than 7.5% at December&nbsp;28, 2002, and has no direct
representation on the Company's Board of Directors. As a result, CSFB is no longer considered an affiliate of the Company. As of December&nbsp;28, 2002, Duane Reade operated 228 drug stores
throughout New York City and the surrounding metropolitan areas of New York and northeastern New Jersey. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Significant
accounting policies followed in the preparation of the Consolidated Financial Statements are as follows: </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Principles of consolidation:</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Consolidated Financial Statements include the accounts of the
Company and its subsidiaries. All significant intercompany transactions and balances have been eliminated. Certain prior year amounts have been reclassified to conform to the current year
presentation. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The
Company has no assets or operations other than its investment in its subsidiary guarantors. Accordingly, the Consolidated Financial Statements present the combined assets and
operations of the subsidiary guarantors. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Reporting year:</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The fiscal year for the Company is the 52- or 53-week reporting period ending on the
last Saturday in December. The 2002 and 2001 fiscal years contain 52 weeks, while the 2000 fiscal year contains 53 weeks. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Cash and cash equivalents:</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Cash and cash equivalents include short-term highly liquid
investments in AAA-rated money market funds, with a maturity of three months or less from the date of acquisition. The Company places its temporary cash in short-term
investments with various financial institutions and limits the amount of credit exposure to any one institution. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Receivables:</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Receivables consist primarily of amounts due from various insurance companies and
governmental agencies under third party payment plans for prescription sales and amounts due from vendors, a majority of which relate to promotional programs. The Company's accounting policy, which is
based on its past collection experience, is to fully reserve for all unpaid pharmacy receivables over 120&nbsp;days old, as well as any others deemed potentially uncollectible. The Company has
provided an allowance for doubtful accounts of $5.0&nbsp;million and $2.5&nbsp;million at December&nbsp;28, 2002 and December&nbsp;29, 2001 respectively. The carrying value of the Company's
receivables approximates fair value given the short-term maturity of these financial instruments. </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>35</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<!-- ZEQ.=1,SEQ=35,EFW="2106462",CP="DUANE READE INC.",DN="1",CHK=86394,FOLIO='35',FILE='DISK030:[03NYC7.03NYC3347]FJ3347A.;28',USER='SMENEZE',CD='28-MAR-2003;12:44' -->
<A NAME="page_fj3347_1_36"> </A>
<BR>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Inventories and cost of sales:</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In fiscal 2000 and 2001, inventories are stated at the lower of cost
or market with cost determined using the retail dollar based first in, first out ("FIFO") method. In fiscal 2002, inventories are stated at the lower of cost or market with cost determined using the
specific cost last in, first out ("LIFO") method. When appropriate, provision is made for obsolete, slow-moving or damaged inventory. At December&nbsp;28, 2002, inventories would
approximate their recorded value if they were valued at the lower of specific first in, first out cost or market. The Company's primary pharmaceutical supplier provides $30.0&nbsp;million of
inventory on a consignment basis. Prescription drug inventory over the consignment limit is accounted for as owned inventory and is included on the Company's balance sheet at LIFO cost. As of
December&nbsp;28, 2002 and December&nbsp;29, 2001, there was approximately $24.8&nbsp;million and $16.4&nbsp;million of prescription drug inventory over the $30.0&nbsp;million consignment
limit included in the Company's consolidated balance sheets. Cost of sales includes all store occupancy related costs and expenses, consisting of lease and sublease related income and expenses, other
recurring real estate related income and expenses primarily from sales and terminations of leases related to store closings and relocations, sales of market related data, store utility costs and
warehouse expenses and distribution costs. The Company reflects promotional allowances from vendors as a reduction of cost of sales or advertising expense, depending on the nature of the allowance,
when such advertising or promotions have been completed and the related allowances have been earned. Other recurring real
estate related income and income from sales of market related data amounted to approximately $5.5&nbsp;million in 2002 compared to $10.6&nbsp;million in 2001. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Property and equipment:</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Property and equipment are stated at cost. Depreciation and amortization are
calculated using the straight-line method over estimated useful lives of assets as follows: </FONT></P>

<!-- User-specified TAGGED TABLE -->
<TABLE WIDTH="76%" BORDER=0 CELLSPACING=0 CELLPADDING=0>
<TR BGCOLOR="#CCEEFF" VALIGN="TOP">
<TD WIDTH="49%"><FONT SIZE=2>Buildings and improvements</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="3%"><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="49%"><FONT SIZE=2>30 years</FONT></TD>
</TR>
<TR BGCOLOR="White" VALIGN="TOP">
<TD WIDTH="49%"><FONT SIZE=2>Furniture, fixtures and equipment</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="3%"><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="49%"><FONT SIZE=2>5-10 years</FONT></TD>
</TR>
<TR BGCOLOR="#CCEEFF" VALIGN="TOP">
<TD WIDTH="49%"><FONT SIZE=2>Computer equipment</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="3%"><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="49%"><FONT SIZE=2>5-7 years</FONT></TD>
</TR>
<TR BGCOLOR="White" VALIGN="TOP">
<TD WIDTH="49%"><FONT SIZE=2>Leasehold improvements</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="3%"><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="49%"><FONT SIZE=2>Life of lease or, if shorter, remaining asset life</FONT></TD>
</TR>
</TABLE>
<!-- end of user-specified TAGGED TABLE -->


<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Other assets:</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Deferred financing costs are amortized using the interest method, over the term of the
underlying debt. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Pharmacy
file and lease acquisition costs are amortized over seven years and the remaining life of the lease, respectively. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Systems
development costs, relating to management information systems, are amortized using the straight-line method over a period of seven years. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Intangible assets:</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The carrying values of goodwill, identifiable intangibles and
long-lived fixed assets are periodically reviewed and evaluated by the Company when events and circumstances indicate that the carrying amount of these assets may not be recoverable. For
intangible assets (excluding goodwill) and long-lived fixed assets, this evaluation is based on the expected future undiscounted operating cash flows of the related assets. Should such
evaluation result in the Company concluding that the carrying amount of identifiable intangibles or fixed assets has been impaired, an appropriate write-down would be recorded. Goodwill is
evaluated at least annually, based upon the market capitalization of the Company's common stock, as specified in Financial Accounting Standards Board Pronouncement No.&nbsp;142 (FAS&nbsp;142),
"Goodwill and Other Intangible Assets". Should the results of this test indicate the existence of impairment, an appropriate write-down would be recorded. During the </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>36</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<!-- ZEQ.=2,SEQ=36,EFW="2106462",CP="DUANE READE INC.",DN="1",CHK=855265,FOLIO='36',FILE='DISK030:[03NYC7.03NYC3347]FJ3347A.;28',USER='SMENEZE',CD='28-MAR-2003;12:44' -->
<A NAME="page_fj3347_1_37"> </A>
<BR>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>
2001 fiscal year, the Company adopted FAS&nbsp;142 for goodwill related to acquisitions completed after June&nbsp;30, 2001. Under this pronouncement, non-impaired goodwill for
acquisitions completed after June&nbsp;30, 2001 is no longer amortized. Beginning in 2002, the Company adopted the provisions of FAS&nbsp;142 for goodwill acquired prior to July&nbsp;1, 2001
and, accordingly, no longer amortizes any of the goodwill recorded in its financial statements. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Revenue recognition:</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company recognizes revenues from the sale of merchandise at the time that
the merchandise is sold. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Advertising expenses:</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Costs incurred to produce media advertising are charged to expense when the
advertising takes place. For the fiscal years ended December&nbsp;28, 2002, December&nbsp;29, 2001 and December&nbsp;30, 2000, advertising expense amounted to $9.0&nbsp;million,
$10.9&nbsp;million and $8.3&nbsp;million, respectively. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Pre-opening expenses:</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Store pre-opening costs, other than capital
expenditures, are expensed when incurred. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Income taxes:</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Income taxes are accounted for under the liability method prescribed by Statement of
Financial Accounting Standards No.&nbsp;109. Deferred tax assets and liabilities are determined based on the difference between the book and tax bases of the respective assets and liabilities as
well as for the deferred tax effects of tax credit carryforwards. Deferred tax assets and liabilities are measured using the enacted tax rates expected to apply to taxable income in the years in which
these temporary differences are expected to be recovered or settled. Valuation allowances are established when management determines that it is more likely than not that a deferred tax asset will not
be realized. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Change of accounting method:</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;As of December&nbsp;30, 2001, the Company adopted a change in
accounting method to convert from the retail dollar first-in, first-out ("FIFO") method to a specific cost based last-in, first-out ("LIFO") method.
Adoption of the specific cost LIFO method will more accurately value inventory by eliminating the averaging inherent in the retail method. In addition, the specific cost LIFO method will reflect the
impact of inflation in the Company's gross margin. The effect of changing from the retail method to the specific cost method was a reduction in inventory of $16.0&nbsp;million, resulting in a
cumulative effect of an accounting change as of December&nbsp;30, 2001 of approximately $9.3&nbsp;million, net of an income tax benefit of $6.7&nbsp;million ($0.39 per basic common share and
$0.38 per diluted common share, respectively). The cumulative effect of changing from FIFO to LIFO on periods prior to December&nbsp;30, 2001 cannot be determined. Pro forma effects of the change
for prior periods have not been presented as cost information is not determinable. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Recently issued accounting standards:</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;During the third quarter of 2001, the Company adopted Financial
Accounting Standards Board Pronouncements Nos. 141 (FAS&nbsp;141) and 142 (FAS&nbsp;142), "Business
Combinations" and "Goodwill and Other Intangible Assets," respectively, for acquisitions completed after June&nbsp;30, 2001. This adoption eliminated goodwill amortization for these acquisitions and
did not have a material impact on the Company's financial position, results of operations or cash flows. Beginning in fiscal 2002, the application of these pronouncements also eliminated amortization
of goodwill for acquisitions completed prior to July&nbsp;1, 2001. As a result, total Company amortization expense for 2002 was reduced by approximately $4.3&nbsp;million. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;During
the first quarter of 2002, the Company adopted Financial Accounting Standards Board Pronouncement No.&nbsp;144 (FAS&nbsp;144), "Accounting for the Impairment or Disposal of
Long-Lived Assets." FAS&nbsp;144 supersedes FAS&nbsp;121, "Accounting for the Impairment of Long-Lived Assets and for Long-Lived Assets to be Disposed of." The
provisions of FAS&nbsp;144 are effective for financial statements issued after December&nbsp;15, 2001. This adoption did not have a material impact on the Company's results of operations,
financial position or cash flows. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In
April&nbsp;2002, FAS No.&nbsp;145, "Rescission of FASB Statements No.&nbsp;4, 44, and 64, Amendment of FASB Statement No.&nbsp;13, and Technical Corrections," was issued.
Under FAS No.&nbsp;145, gains and losses related to the extinguishment of debt should no longer be segregated on the income statement as extraordinary items. Instead, such gains and losses should be
included as a component of income from continuing operations. The provisions of FAS No.&nbsp;145 are effective for fiscal years beginning after May&nbsp;15, 2002 with early adoption encouraged.
Upon adoption, the Company will reclassify from extraordinary charges to other income / (loss), for the fiscal years ended December&nbsp;28, 2002 and </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>38</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<!-- ZEQ.=4,SEQ=38,EFW="2106462",CP="DUANE READE INC.",DN="1",CHK=1047728,FOLIO='38',FILE='DISK030:[03NYC7.03NYC3347]FJ3347A.;28',USER='SMENEZE',CD='28-MAR-2003;12:44' -->
<A NAME="page_fj3347_1_39"> </A>
<BR>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>
December&nbsp;29, 2001, pre-tax amounts of $11.4&nbsp;million and $2.6&nbsp;million, respectively. The income tax provisions for the 2002 and 2001 fiscal years will be adjusted
commensurately. Reported net income will remain unaffected by the reclassification. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In
July&nbsp;2002, FAS No.&nbsp;146, "Accounting for Costs Associated with Exit or Disposal Activities," was issued. This statement nullifies Emerging Issues Task Force (EITF) Issue
No.&nbsp;94-3, "Liability Recognition for Certain Employee Termination Benefits and Other Costs to Exit an Activity (including Certain Costs Incurred in a Restructuring)." FAS
No.&nbsp;146 requires that a liability for costs associated with an exit or disposal activity be recognized when the liability is incurred. The provisions of FAS No.&nbsp;146 are effective for
exit or disposal activities initiated after December&nbsp;31, 2002, with early adoption encouraged. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In
September&nbsp;2002, the Emerging Issues Task Force released Issue No.&nbsp;02-16, "Accounting by a Reseller for Cash Consideration Received from a Vendor". The
pronouncement addresses two issues. The first issue requires that vendor allowances be categorized as a reduction of cost of sales unless they are a reimbursement of costs incurred to sell the
vendor's products, in which case, the cash consideration should be characterized as a reduction of that cost. Cash consideration received from a vendor in excess of the fair value of the benefit
received should be characterized as a reduction of cost of sales. As required, the Company will adopt this portion of the pronouncement in 2003. The second issue requires that rebates or refunds
payable only if the customer completes a specified cumulative level of purchases should be recognized as a reduction of cost of sales based on a systematic and rational allocation over the purchase
period. This portion of the pronouncement is to be applied to all new arrangements initiated after November&nbsp;21, 2002. The Company does not expect that the adoption of this pronouncement will
have a material impact on the Company's consolidated results of operations, financial position, or cash flows. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In
November&nbsp;2002, the Financial Accounting Standards Board issued FASB Interpretation (FIN) No.&nbsp;45, "Guarantor's Accounting and Disclosure Requirements for Guarantees,
Including Indirect Guarantees of Indebtedness of Others." FIN No.&nbsp;45 clarifies the requirements of FAS No.&nbsp;5, "Accounting for Contingencies," relating to a guarantor's accounting for and
disclosure of, the issuance of certain types of guarantees. FIN No.&nbsp;45 elaborates on the existing disclosure requirements for most guarantees, including loan guarantees such as standby letters
of credit. It also clarifies that at the time a company issues a guarantee, the company must recognize an initial liability for the fair value, or market value, of the obligations it assumes under the
guarantee and must disclose that information in its interim and annual financial statements. The provisions related to recognizing a liability at inception of the guarantee for the fair value of the
guarantor's obligations does not apply to product warranties or to guarantees accounted for as derivatives. The recognition provisions of FIN No.&nbsp;45 are effective for the Company beginning
January&nbsp;1, 2003. This interpretation is not expected to have a material impact on the Company's financial position, results of operations or cash flows. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In
December&nbsp;2002, SFAS No.&nbsp;148, "Accounting for Stock-Based Compensation&#151;Transition and Disclosure" was issued. This statement provides alternative methods of
transition for a voluntary change to the fair value based method of accounting for stock-based employee compensation. In addition, this statement amends the disclosure requirements of SFAS
No.&nbsp;123 to require prominent disclosures about the
method of accounting for stock-based compensation and the effect of the method used on reported results. As required, the Company adopted SFAS No.&nbsp;148 effective in 2002. The </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>39</FONT></P>

<A NAME="page_fj3347_1_40"> </A>
<BR>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>
adoption did not have a material impact on the Company's consolidated results of operations, financial position, or cash flows. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In
January&nbsp;2003, the Financial Accounting Standards Board issued FIN No.&nbsp;46, "Consolidation of Variable Interest Entities." FIN No.&nbsp;46 requires a variable interest
entity to be consolidated by a company if that company is subject to a majority of the risk of loss from the variable interest entity's activities or entitled to receive a majority of the entity's
residual returns or both. The consolidation requirements of FIN No.&nbsp;46 apply immediately to variable interest entities created after January&nbsp;31, 2003. The consolidation requirements
apply to older entities in the first fiscal year or interim period beginning after June&nbsp;15, 2003. Certain of the disclosure requirements apply in all financial statements issued after
January&nbsp;31, 2003, regardless of when the variable interest entity was established. The adoption of these provisions is not anticipated to have a material impact on the Company's financial
position, results of operations or cash flows. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Employee stock option plans:</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;At December&nbsp;28, 2002, the Company has two stock-based employee

</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> and related Interpretations. There is no stock-based employee compensation cost reflected in net income, as
